ENTRY       EC 6.4.1.2                  Enzyme
NAME        acetyl-CoA carboxylase;
            HFA1 (gene name);
            ACC1 (gene name);
            acetyl coenzyme A carboxylase;
            acetyl-CoA:carbon-dioxide ligase (ADP-forming)
CLASS       Ligases;
            Forming carbon-carbon bonds;
            Ligases that form carbon-carbon bonds (only sub-subclass identified to date)
SYSNAME     acetyl-CoA:hydrogencarbonate ligase (ADP-forming)
REACTION    ATP + acetyl-CoA + hydrogencarbonate = ADP + phosphate + malonyl-CoA [RN:R00742]
ALL_REAC    R00742
SUBSTRATE   ATP [CPD:C00002];
            acetyl-CoA [CPD:C00024];
            hydrogencarbonate [CPD:C00288]
PRODUCT     ADP [CPD:C00008];
            phosphate [CPD:C00009];
            malonyl-CoA [CPD:C00083]
COMMENT     This enzyme is a multi-domain polypeptide that catalyses three different activities - a biotin carboxyl-carrier protein (BCCP), a biotin carboxylase that catalyses the transfer of a carboxyl group from hydrogencarbonate to the biotin molecule carried by the carrier protein, and the transfer of the carboxyl group from biotin to acetyl-CoA, forming malonyl-CoA. In some organisms these activities are catalysed by separate enzymes (see EC 6.3.4.14, biotin carboxylase, and EC 2.1.3.15, acetyl-CoA carboxytransferase). The carboxylation of the carrier protein requires ATP, while the transfer of the carboxyl group to acetyl-CoA does not.
HISTORY     EC 6.4.1.2 created 1961, modified 2018
